Second Category of Fasts: Intention Requirements (Tabyit and Ta'yin)
Lists fasts requiring nighttime specific intention and details intention rules

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which fasts require a specified intention made at night (tabyit and ta'yin) and apply the Hanafi rules regarding intention continuity, retraction, and the effect of saying 'in sha Allah' on intention validity.

Core Idea
Qada, kaffarah, and absolute vows require intention at night; mere retraction or saying 'in sha Allah' does not necessarily invalidate.

In the previous section, we covered the first category of fasts (Ramadan and nafl) where intention does not need to be specified or made at night. Now we delve into the second category: fasts that require both tabyit (nighttime intention) and ta'yin (specification). These include qada of Ramadan, qada of spoiled nafl, all kaffarah fasts, and absolute vows. The Hanafi school provides detailed rules about the intention itself—its nature, continuity, and the effect of common utterances like 'in sha Allah'. Understanding these rules is essential for correctly performing these obligatory fasts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fasts in the second category
List the fasts that require tabyit and ta'yin as per the text: qada of Ramadan, qada of spoiled nafl, kaffarat (all types), and absolute vows (nadhr mutlaq).
These are distinct from Ramadan and nafl, which do not require specification or nighttime intention.
2
Understand the definition and components of intention
Intention (niyyah) is a firm resolve in the heart. The scholars recommend uttering it, but it is not obligatory. Continuity (al-baqā' ʿalayhā) is required—if one retracts at night, the intention is nullified and he is not considered fasting.
Retraction can be remedied by renewing the intention at the proper time (e.g., by passing time in a state suitable for fasting).
3
Analyze the 'in sha Allah' issue
If one says 'I intend to fast tomorrow if Allah wills', the relied-upon view (istihsan) is that the intention is valid because it is seeking divine help, not a true exception. If meant as a true exception, the intention is invalid.
The difference from divorce is that exception is a verbal act affecting verbal rulings; intention is a heart act, not affected by tongue.
4
Examine the rules for combining intentions
If one combines qada and nafl intentions, according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf it counts as qada (wajib overrides nafl); according to Muhammad it counts as nafl. If one combines two contradictory wajibs (e.g., qada of Ramadan and kaffarah), neither is valid and it becomes nafl.
This shows the importance of specifying a single clear intention for obligatory fasts.
5
Understand the case of al-zann (mistaken obligation)
If someone starts fasting thinking it is obligatory, then learns it is not, and breaks after some time, qada is required because he chose to continue. This applies when the mistake is realized at the time of intention.
This is an exception: qada is not required if he breaks immediately upon learning.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القسم الثاني، وهو ما يُشترط له تعيين النية، وتبييتها فهو قضاء رمضان، وقضاء ما أفسدَهُ من نَفْلِ. وَصَوْمُ الكفَّارَاتِ بأنواعها. والنَّدْرُ المُطْلَقُ، كقوله: إن شفى الله مريضي فعلي صوم يوم، فحصل الشفاء. ثم اعلم بأن النية جزم بالقلب على ما يريد الإتيان به من الصوم، واستحب المشايخ التلفظ بها، ويشترط في النية البقاء عليها، فلو رجع عما نوى ليلاً لم يصر صائماً، ولو أفطر لا شيء عليه إلا القضاء في رمضان والمنذور، لأن تلك النية انتقضت بالرجوع عنها، إلا أن يعود إلى تجديد النية، ويجعل مضيه فيه في وقتها تجديداً لها، وبه صرح في الحافظية، كذا في شرح المقدسي، وفي النهاية: إذا قال: نويت أن أصوم غداً إن شاء الله تعالى، أو قال: أصوم غداً إن شاء الله فلا رواية في هذه المسألة عن أصحابنا، وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني رحمه الله: فيها قياس واستحسان، فالقياس أن لا يصير صائماً؛ لأن بالاستثناء تبطل النية، وفي الاستحسان يصير صائماً، وفي الظهيرية: هو الصحيح لأن قوله: إن شاء الله ها هنا ليس في معنى حقيقة الاستثناء، بل هو على معنى الاستعانة وطلب التوفيق من الله تعالى، حتى لو أراد به حقيقة الاستثناء نقول أنه لا يصير صائماً بهذه النية، كذا في التاتارخانية بخلاف الطلاق وغيره، والفقه في الفرق أن الاستثناء عمل اللسان، فيبطل ما يتعلق باللسان من الأحكام كالطلاق، وأما النية فعمل القلب لا تعلق لها باللسان، فلا تبطل بالاستثناء الذي هو عمل اللسان، كذا في التجنيس والذخيرة ولو نوى الفطر لم يكن مفطراً، ولو نوى التكلم في الصلاة ولم يتكلم لم تفسد صلاته، خلافاً للشافعي فيهما، ولو جمع ليلاً بين نية القضاء والتطوع يقع قضاء عندهما؛ لأنه لا معارضة بين الواجب والنفل، وعند محمد يقع تطوعاً، ولو نوى قضاء رمضان وكفارة اليمين لا يصير شارعاً في واحد منهما بالإجماع للتعارض، ولكن يصير متطوعاً، ولو أفسده لا يلزمه القضاء؛ لأنه شرع فيه على قصد إسقاط الواجب، وإذا نوى الصوم للقضاء بعد طلوع الفجر لا يصح نيته عن القضاء، وإن أفطر لزمه القضاء، كما إذا تطوع ابتداء، وهذا يرد إشكالاً على مسألة المظنون، كذا في التجنيس والمزيد. والظان هو من دخل في الصوم على حسبان أنه عليه ثم علم أنه لم يكن عليه فأفطر عليه القضاء، لأنه مضى عليه ساعة، فقد اختار المضى عليه فوجب عليه، لكن هذا إذا تبين له ذلك في وقت النية كما في الفتاوى الصغرى والجامع.
As for the second category, which requires specifying the intention and making it at night: it is qada of Ramadan, qada of what one spoiled of nafl, fasts of kaffarat of all kinds, and the absolute vow, like his saying: 'If Allah heals my sick, then upon me is to fast a day,' and healing occurs. Then know that intention is a resolve in the heart for what one intends to do of fasting, and the scholars recommended uttering it, and continuity of intention is required. So if he retracts from what he intended at night, he does not become a faster, and if he breaks the fast, nothing is upon him except qada in Ramadan and the vowed [fast] because that intention is nullified by retraction, unless he returns to renew the intention and makes his passing of it at its time a renewal, as stated in al-Hafiziyyah, as in Sharh al-Maqdisi. And in al-Nihayah: if he says, 'I intend to fast tomorrow if Allah wills,' or says, 'I will fast tomorrow if Allah wills,' there is no narration about this issue from our companions. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: there is qiyas and istihsan in it; by qiyas he does not become a faster because the exception nullifies the intention, and by istihsan he becomes a faster. In al-Zuhayriyyah: the correct view is that he becomes a faster because his saying 'if Allah wills' here is not in the sense of true exception but is in the sense of seeking help and asking for success from Allah, so if he intended a true exception, we say he does not become a faster with this intention, as in al-Tatarakhaniyyah, unlike divorce and other matters. And the fiqh of the difference is that exception is an action of the tongue, so it nullifies what pertains to the tongue of rulings like divorce. As for intention, it is an action of the heart, it has no connection to the tongue, so it is not nullified by exception which is an action of the tongue, as in al-Tajnīs and al-Dhakhirah. And if he intended to break the fast, he is not a breaker; and if he intended to speak in prayer and did not speak, his prayer is not invalidated, contrary to al-Shafi'i in both. And if he combined at night between intention of qada and nafl, it falls as qada according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad] because there is no opposition between wajib and nafl; according to Muhammad it falls as nafl. And if he intended qada of Ramadan and kaffarah of oath, he does not become a starter of either by consensus due to conflict, but he becomes a volunteer. And if he spoils it, qada is not binding on him because he started it with the intention of discharging an obligation. And if he intends fasting for qada after dawn, his intention for qada is not valid, and if he breaks the fast, qada is binding on him, just as if he initially volunteered. And this presents a difficulty for the issue of al-zann, as in al-Tajnīs and al-Mazīd. And al-zann is the one who enters into a fast thinking it is binding on him, then learns it was not binding, then breaks the fast; qada is binding on him because an hour has passed, and he has chosen to continue it, so it becomes obligatory. But this is when it becomes clear to him at the time of intention, as in al-Fatawa al-Sughra and al-Jami'.
Source pages p. 626

Commentary
This passage first lists the second category of fasts that require both a specified intention (ta'yin al-niyyah) and that the intention be made at night (tabyit). These include: qada of Ramadan, qada of a spoiled nafl fast, all types of kaffarat (e.g., for oath, zihar, killing, breaking fast in Ramadan, etc.), and absolute vows (nadhrmutlaq) not tied to a specific time. The author then explains detailed rules of intention. Intention is a firm resolve in the heart; vocal utterance is recommended but not required. The intention must persist; if one retracts it at night, he is not considered fasting, and breaking it requires qada only for Ramadan and vows. Retraction nullifies the intention, but one can renew it by the same act of passing time in the fasting period. The issue of saying 'in sha Allah' in intention: there is no explicit narration from the early Hanafi masters. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani says by qiyas (analogy) the intention is nullified, but by istihsan (juristic preference) it is valid because 'in sha Allah' is not a true exception but a request for divine help. The relied-upon view (in al-Zuhayriyyah) is that it is valid. The difference from divorce is that exception is a verbal act affecting verbal rulings; intention is a heart act. Additional points: intending to break the fast does not break it; intending to speak in prayer without speaking does not invalidate it (contrary to al-Shafi'i). If one combines qada and nafl intentions at night, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it counts as qada (wajib overrides nafl), while Muhammad alone says it counts as nafl. If one intends two contradictory wajibs (qada of Ramadan and kaffarah), consensus says neither is valid; it becomes a nafl. If one intends qada after dawn, it is invalid as qada; if he breaks, qada is still required. The case of al-zann (someone who mistakenly thinks a fast is obligatory, starts it, then learns it's not): if he breaks after some time, qada is obligatory because he chose to continue, but only if the mistake is realized at the time of intention.

Key Terms
تعيين النية (taʿyīn al-niyyah): Specifying the type of fast (e.g., qada of Ramadan, kaffarah) in the intention.
تبييت النية (tabyīt al-niyyah): Making the intention during the night before dawn for the fast of the following day.
النذر المطلق (al-nadhr al-muṭlaq): An absolute vow not tied to a specific time, e.g., 'I vow to fast a day' without specifying when.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The intention is invalid because it includes an exception.
B) The intention is valid and he becomes a faster, regardless of his inner intent.
C) The intention is valid unless he meant it as a true exception; otherwise it is valid.
D) The fast is valid but he must repeat it with a proper intention.

Key Takeaway
Fasts of qada, kaffarah, and absolute vows require a specified intention at night; the intention is an act of the heart and is not invalidated by common utterances like 'in sha Allah' unless truly meant as an exception.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
The Effect of 'In sha Allah' on Fasting Intention
Expansion on the ruling of istithna' in fasting intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on saying 'in sha Allah' in the fasting intention and explain why it does not invalidate the fast, including the distinction between heart and tongue acts.

Core Idea
Saying 'in sha Allah' in intention does not invalidate the fast because intention is a heart act, unaffected by tongue.

When fasting, Muslims often say 'in sha Allah' after expressing their intention. Does this conditional statement invalidate the fast? The Hanafi school provides a nuanced answer based on the nature of intention as an act of the heart, distinguishing it from verbal acts like divorce. This lesson examines the Hanafi position, its proof, and how it contrasts with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize the question: does saying 'I intend to fast tomorrow if Allah wills' affect the validity of the fast? Note that there is no explicit narration from early Hanafi authorities on this precise scenario.
2
Apply qiyas vs istihsan
Al-Hulwani presents two approaches: by qiyas, the exception invalidates the intention; by istihsan (juristic preference), the phrase is not a real exception but a plea for divine help, so the fast is valid.
The correct view is istihsan, as recorded in al-Zahiriyya.
3
Understand the heart/tongue distinction
Intention is an act of the heart, while the exception is an act of the tongue. Tongue acts do not affect heart acts. Contrast with divorce: divorce is a tongue act, so exception can nullify it.
This distinction is key to the Hanafi position.
4
Contrast with Shafi'i on intention to break
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that merely intending to break the fast or speak in prayer invalidates the act. Hanafis disagree: only actual action (eating, speaking) breaks the fast or prayer.
The same heart/tongue principle applies: intention alone does not constitute action.
5
Derive the practical ruling
The fast is valid with 'in sha Allah'. If someone genuinely intended a real exception (rare), it may invalidate, but the default is istihsan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقتها تجديداً لها، وبه صرح في « الحافظية»، كذا في شرح المقدسي»، وفي «النهاية » : إذا قال: نويت أن أصوم غداً إن شاء الله تعالى، أو قال: أصوم غداً إن شاء الله فلا رواية في هذه المسألة عن أصحابنا، وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني رحمه الله : فيها قياس واستحسان، فالقياس أن لا يصير صائماً؛ لأن بالاستثناء تبطل النية، وفي الاستحسان يصير صائماً، وفي « الظهيرية»: هو الصحيح لأن قوله: إن شاء الله ها هنا ليس في معنى حقيقة الاستثناء، بل هو على معنى الاستعانة وطلب التوفيق من الله تعالى، حتى لو أراد به حقيقة الاستثناء نقول أنه لا يصير صائماً بهذه النية، كذا في التاتارخانية بخلاف الطلاق وغيره، والفقه في الفرق أن الاستثناء عمل اللسان، فيبطل ما يتعلق باللسان من الأحكام كالطلاق، وأما النية فعمل القلب لا تعلق لها باللسان، فلا تبطل بالاستثناء الذي هو عمل اللسان، كذا في التجنيس والذخيرة ولو نوى الفطر لم يكن مفطراً، ولو نوى التكلم في الصلاة ولم يتكلم لم تفسد صلاته، خلافاً للشافعي فيهما، ولو جمع ليلاً بين نية القضاء والتطوع يقع قضاء عندهما؛ لأنه لا معارضة بين الواجب والنفل، وعند محمد يقع تطوعاً، ولو نوى قضاء رمضان وكفارة اليمين لا يصير شارعاً في واحد منهما بالإجماع للتعارض، ولكن يصير متطوعاً، ولو أفسده لا يلزمه القضاء؛ لأنه شرع فيه على قصد إسقاط الواجب، وإذا نوى الصوم للقضاء بعد طلوع الفجر لا يصح نيته عن القضاء، وإن أفطر لزمه القضاء، كما إذا تطوع ابتداء، وهذا يرد إشكالاً على مسألة المظنون، كذا في التجنيس والمزيد . والظان هو من دخل في الصوم على حسبان أنه عليه ثم علم أنه لم يكن عليه فأفطر عليه القضاء، لأنه مضى عليه ساعة، فقد اختار المضي عليه فوجب عليه، لكن هذا إذا تبين له ذلك في وقت النية كما في الفتاوى الصغرى والجامع.
Renewing it at its time, and it is stated explicitly in 'al-Hafiziyya', similarly in 'Sharh al-Maqdisi', and in 'al-Nihaya': If he said: 'I intend to fast tomorrow if Allah wills' or he said: 'I will fast tomorrow if Allah wills', there is no narration from our companions on this issue. Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani (may Allah have mercy on him) said: There is qiyas and istihsan in it. By qiyas, he does not become a fasting person because the exception invalidates the intention; by istihsan, he becomes a fasting person. In 'al-Zahiriyya': The correct view is that his saying 'if Allah wills' here is not in the sense of a real exception, but rather in the sense of seeking help and asking for success from Allah Almighty. Even if he intended it as a real exception, we would say he does not become a fasting person with this intention, as in 'al-Tatarkhaniyya', contrary to divorce and other matters. The juristic reasoning for the difference is that the exception is an act of the tongue, so it invalidates matters related to the tongue such as divorce. As for intention, it is an act of the heart, not related to the tongue, so it is not invalidated by the exception which is an act of the tongue, as in 'al-Tajnis' and 'al-Dhakhira'. If he intended to break the fast, he does not become a breaker. If he intended to speak in prayer but did not speak, his prayer is not invalidated, contrary to al-Shafi'i in both cases. If he combined at night the intention of qada and tatawwu', it falls as qada according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because there is no conflict between obligatory and supererogatory; according to Muhammad, it falls as tatawwu'. If he intended qada of Ramadan and expiation of an oath, he does not enter into either by consensus due to conflict, but becomes a mutatawwi'. If he invalidates it, qada is not incumbent upon him because he entered with the intention of fulfilling an obligation. If he intends fasting for qada after dawn, his intention for qada is not valid, and if he breaks his fast, qada is incumbent upon him, just as if he started as a tatawwu'. This rebuts an objection to the issue of al-maznun, as in 'al-Tajnis' and 'al-Mazid'. Al-maznun is one who enters into fasting assuming it is obligatory upon him, then learns it is not, and then breaks his fast; qada is incumbent upon him because he has passed an hour, so he has chosen to continue, so it becomes obligatory. But this applies when it becomes clear to him at the time of intention, as in 'al-Fatawa al-Sughra' and 'al-Jami'.
Source pages p. 627

Commentary
This passage, drawn from multiple Hanafi sources, discusses several nuanced issues related to the intention (niyyah) for fasting. The first issue concerns making an exception (istithna') with 'in sha Allah' when verbalizing the intention. The commentators explain that there is no explicit narration from the early Hanafi authorities, but Shams al-A'imma al-Hulwani presents two possible approaches: qiyas (analogy) would invalidate the intention because exceptions nullify the act, but istihsan (juristic preference) upholds the intention because the phrase here is not a genuine exception but a plea for divine assistance. This view is deemed correct in al-Zahiriyya. The reasoning is that intention is an act of the heart, unaffected by verbal acts like exceptions, unlike divorce where a verbal exception can nullify the pronouncement. Next, the text clarifies that merely intending to break the fast does not actually break it, nor does intending to speak in prayer invalidate the prayer unless speech occurs, contradicting Imam al-Shafi'i who holds that intention alone suffices to invalidate. Then, combining intentions at night: according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), combining qada (make-up) and tatawwu' (voluntary) intentions results in qada because the obligatory takes precedence; but Imam Muhammad alone holds that it becomes tatawwu'. Combining qada and kaffarah (expiation) intentions is invalid due to conflict, resulting in tatawwu'. If such a fast is invalidated, no qada is required because the entry was for obligation. Lastly, the issue of al-maznun: if one mistakenly thinks a fast is obligatory and begins with that intention, then discovers it is not, and breaks the fast, qada is required if he had time to reconsider at the moment of intention. The text is technical and assumes familiarity with prior rulings.

Key Terms
النية (al-niyyah): The intention in the heart to perform an act of worship; it is a condition for the validity of fasting.
الاستثناء (al-istithnā'): Verbal exception using phrases like 'in sha Allah' when expressing intention; here it is considered not a real exception but a plea for divine help.
الظان (al-ẓānn): One who mistakenly believes a fast is obligatory upon him and begins fasting with that intention, then discovers it is not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone intends to fast and says 'in sha Allah', what is the ruling?
A) The fast is invalid because the intention is conditional.
B) The fast is valid because the phrase is not a real exception but a plea for divine help.
C) The fast is invalid only if the person actually means the exception.
D) The fast is valid only if the intention is made at night.

Key Takeaway
Saying 'in sha Allah' in the intention for fasting does not invalidate the fast because the phrase is a plea for help, and intention is an act of the heart, unaffected by the tongue.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
7 min
Establishing the Crescent of Ramadan and the Ruling on the Day of Doubt
Defines how Ramadan is proven and the ruling on fasting the day of doubt.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of establishing Ramadan, define the day of doubt, and apply the Hanafi ruling that fasting it is makruh except for a firmly intended nafl fast.

Core Idea
Ramadan starts only with sighting or completing 30 days; the day of doubt is prohibited for obligatory fasts but allowed for a firm nafl.

This lesson covers two interconnected rulings: how we know Ramadan has begun, and what to do on the confusing day that may be the last of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan. The Hanafi school heeds a clear prophetic directive: base the month on actual sighting, not calculations, and treat the day of doubt with caution except for those who firmly intend a voluntary fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify how Ramadan is established
From the text, Ramadan is proven either by sighting the crescent (ru'yah) on the 29th of Sha'ban, or by completing 30 days of Sha'ban if the crescent is obscured. This is based on the hadith.
Note the collective duty (fard kifayah) to seek the crescent at sunset on the 29th.
2
Define the day of doubt
The day of doubt is the 30th day of Sha'ban when the crescent is not seen due to an obstruction (cloud, dust, etc.), leaving uncertainty whether it is still Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan.
The text defines it as a day where knowledge and ignorance are equal.
3
Understand the ruling on fasting the day of doubt
Every fast on this day is disliked (makruh) whether it is obligatory (fard), mandatory (wajib), or a voluntary fast with hesitation. The only exception is a voluntary (nafl) fast that is firmly intended without any doubt.
The exception applies only when one is certain they are observing nafl, not Ramadan or any other obligatory fast.
4
Analyze the proof
The hadith 'Fast upon seeing it, break upon seeing it, and if obscured, complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty' is the primary evidence. The imperative 'akmilu' indicates that until the count is complete, fasting cannot begin.
The commentary also notes that astrologers' statements carry no weight; only actual sighting matters.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
If someone intended to fast on the day of doubt for Ramadan without certainty, the fast is makruh. If they intended a nafl with firm resolve, it is permissible and not disliked.
This distinction is crucial for practice.

Source Text

(و) بين (يوم الشَّكُ) بقوله : ويوم الشك ( هو : ما يلي التاسع والعشرين من شعبان، وقد استوى فيه طَرَفُ العلمِ والجَهْلِ) بحقيقة الحال ( بأن غُمَّ الهلالُ) أي: هلال رمضان فاحتمل كمال شعبان، أو نقصانه نظراً لقوله : « الشَّهْرُ هَكَذَا وَهَكَذَا وَهَكَذَا وَخَنَسَ إِبْهَامَهُ فِي المَرَّةِ الثَالِثَةِ » (۳)، يعني: تسعة وعشرين وقوله: هكذا وهكذا وهكذا أي من غير خنس يعني: ثلاثين، فيشك بوجود علة، كغيم في اليوم الثلاثين أمن رمضان هو أو من شعبان ، قال ( الكمال » : أو يغم من رجب هلال شعبان فأكملت عدته ولم يكن رؤي هلال رمضان، فيقع الشك في الثلاثين من شعبان، أهو الثلاثون أو الحادي والثلاثون انتهى. وقال الشيخ الإمام بدر الدين رحمه الله: العلة وصف [ يحل ] بالمحل لا عن اختيار، والغيم والغبار والدخان ونحوه، وإن كان عيناً غير أنه يمنع الرائي من المنظور إليه، وهذا عرض على أنه مانع كذا في « المستصفى». Chapter on what establishes the crescent and on fasting the day of doubt and other matters. Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent or by completing thirty days of Sha'ban if the crescent is obscured. The day of doubt is: the day following the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban, where knowledge and ignorance are equal, because the crescent is obscured. Every fast is disliked on it except a nafl fast firmly intended without hesitation between it and another fast... Chapter: It is a collective duty to seek the crescent on the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban at sunset, because it may be twenty-nine. Hence Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent due to his saying, 'Fast upon seeing it, and break the fast upon seeing it, and if it is obscured for you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty days.' So he said 'or by completing thirty days of Sha'ban if the crescent is obscured' because it was not seen due to cloud or similar, as we narrated. This is by consensus. It is disliked to point at the crescent when seeing it because that is a practice of the Jahiliyyah. This indicates that the statements of astrologers are not considered, and the crescent is not established by them, as we will mention. He explained 'the day of doubt' by saying: The day of doubt is: the day following the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban, where knowledge and ignorance are equal regarding the true state, because the crescent is obscured, i.e., the crescent of Ramadan, so it is possible that Sha'ban is complete or incomplete, considering his saying, 'The month is like this, like this, like this,' and he tucked his thumb in the third time, meaning twenty-nine, and his saying 'like this, like this, like this' without tucking means thirty. So there is doubt due to an obstruction like clouds on the thirtieth day: is it of Ramadan or of Sha'ban? Al-Kamal said: Or if the crescent of Sha'ban is obscured from Rajab and its count is completed, and the crescent of Ramadan is not seen, then doubt occurs on the thirtieth of Sha'ban: is it the thirtieth or the thirty-first? The Shaykh al-Imam Badr al-Din (may Allah have mercy on him) said: The obstruction is a description that occurs in a place not by choice, and cloud, dust, smoke and the like, although they are physical objects, prevent the viewer from the viewed; this is an accident as an obstruction, as in al-Mustasfa. 'And it is disliked on it' i.e., the day of doubt, 'every fast of fard or wajib, and a fast in which one hesitates between nafl and other, except a nafl fast firmly intended without hesitation between it and another fast' then...
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Nur al-Idah begins a new chapter on establishing the crescent of Ramadan and the rulings for the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk). The matn states that Ramadan is established either by actual sighting of the crescent or, if the crescent is obscured (by clouds, etc.), by completing thirty days of Sha'ban. This is based on the well-known hadith: 'Fast upon seeing it, break the fast upon seeing it, and if it is obscured, complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty.' The commentary adds that seeking the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban at sunset is a collective obligation (fard kifayah) because it may be that the month is only 29 days. The day of doubt is defined as the day following the 29th of Sha'ban when the crescent is obscured, making it impossible to know whether it is the 30th of Sha'ban or the 1st of Ramadan. The ruling: every fast on this day is disliked (makruh), whether it is a fard (obligatory, e.g., making up a missed Ramadan fast) or wajib (e.g., a vowed fast), or even a nafl fast if one is undecided about its nature. However, a nafl fast that is firmly intended without any hesitation (jazm) between it and another fast is permissible and not disliked. This exception is important: a person may voluntarily fast on the day of doubt if they are certain they intend nafl only, not Ramadan or any other obligation. The commentary also notes that astrologers' predictions are not considered in establishing the crescent, and pointing at the moon during sighting is makruh as it resembles pre-Islamic practices.

Key Terms
الهلال (al-hilāl): The new crescent moon that marks the beginning of a lunar month, specifically here for Ramadan.
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th day of Sha'ban when the crescent is obscured, making it uncertain whether it is still Sha'ban or the first day of Ramadan.
التماس الهلال (iltimās al-hilāl): The collective duty to look for the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban at sunset.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling for fasting on the day of doubt with a firm intention to perform a nafl fast?
A) It is makruh and not permissible.
B) It is permissible and not makruh.
C) It is forbidden (haram).
D) It is recommended (mustahabb).

Key Takeaway
Ramadan must be established by sighting or completing 30 days; the day of doubt is prohibited for obligatory fasts but allowed for a firm nafl.

Establishing the Crescent of Ramadan and the Day of Doubt
Explains the ruling and proof for establishing Ramadan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two methods of establishing Ramadan and define yawm al-shakk according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Ramadan is established by sighting the crescent or completing 30 days; the day of doubt is the 30th when the moon is obscured.

This passage from Nur al-Idah explains how the Islamic calendar determines the start of Ramadan. Understanding these rules is essential for proper observance. The text clarifies that only actual sighting or completing the count of Sha'ban is valid, and it defines the critical day of doubt.

Guided Path
1
Identify the methods of establishing Ramadan
Read the text: Ramadan is established by sighting the crescent (ru'ya) or by completing 30 days of Sha'ban if obscured. Note the hadith as evidence.
The hadith is the primary proof; consensus is also mentioned.
2
Analyze the dalil and its wajh al-dalalah
The imperative 'sūmū' and 'akmilū' indicate obligation (wujub) in Hanafi usul. The phrase 'fa-in ghumma 'alaykum' triggers the completion rule.
The hadith is mutawatir? Actually it's ahad but thubut is qati due to widespread acceptance.
3
Define yawm al-shakk precisely
The text defines it as the day following the 29th of Sha'ban when the crescent is obscured, making knowledge and ignorance equal. It is not the 29th itself.
Distinguish from the common misunderstanding that any uncertain day qualifies.
4
Note the rejection of astrological calculations
The text states that pointing to the moon is disliked and astrologers' statements have no weight; the crescent is only established by sighting or completion.
This is a key difference from some modern practices.

(وكـرة فـيـه) أي: يـوم الشـك (كـل صـوم مــن فـرض وواجب، وصوم ردد فيه بين نفل وغيره ( الأصومَ نَفْلٍ، جَزَم به بلا ترديد بينه وبين صوم آخر) فإنـه
وإن ظهر أنه رمضانَ أجزاً عنه ما صامَهُ.
لا يكره إذا كان على وجه لا يعلم العوام ذلك فيعتادوا صومه فيظنه الجُهَّال زيادة على رمضان كــذا قيده « الكمال » ، وإذا وافق صوماً كان يصومه، فالصوم أفضل بالإجماع، واختلفوا في الأفضل إذا لم يوافق معتاده قيل: الأفضل الفطر احترازاً عن ظاهر النهي ) ، وقيل : الأفضل الصوم، اقتداءً بعائشة وعلي، فإنهما كانا يصومانه (۳)، ثم فيما يكره تتفاوت الكراهة. أما كـراهـة صـومـه عـلـى أنـه مـن رمضان فلقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « مَنْ صَامَ يَوْمَ الشَّكَ، فَقَدْ عَصَى أبَا الْقَاسِمِ (۳) وفيه تشبه بأهل الكتاب في زيادة مدة الصوم، فإن ظهرت رمضانيته أجزأه وإن افطره فظهر من شعبان لم يقضه، كالمظنون لمشروعيته مسقطاً، وأما كراهة الواجب فلصورة النهي كصلاته في أرض الغير، لكن كراهته دون الأول لـعــدم التشبه، ولو ظهر رمضانيته أجزأه لو مقيماً، ولو مسافراً فعن الواجب عند الإمام، ولو ظـهـر مـن شعبان فعماً نوى في الصحيح، وأما كراهة النفل مع الترديد فلأنه ناو للفـرض مـن وجـه، وهـو أن يقول: إن كان غداً من رمضان فعنه وإلا فتطوع، (وإن ظهر ) يوم الشك (أنـه) من (رمضان أجزاً عنه) أي: عن رمضان (ما صامَهُ) بأي نية كانت، إلا أن يكون مسافراً ونواه عن واجــب آخر في الصحيح، كما تقدم لما قلناه ، وإن ظهر من شعبان كان تطوعاً غير مضمون؛ لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته من وجه، وإن ردَّد بين واجب ونفل وظهر من شعبان لم يجز عن الواجب لأن الجهة لم تثبت للتردد فيها، وأصل النية لا يكفيه، ويكون فرضاً غير مضمون بالقضاء، لشروعه فيه مسقطاً، وأما عدم كراهة التطوع الذي جزم به فلقوله ل الرجل : هَلْ صُمْتَ مِنْ سِرَارِ شَعْبَانَ؟ قال: لا، قال: فَإِذَا أفْطَرْتَ فَهُمْ يَوْمَاً مَكَانَهُ ) وسرار الشهر - بالفتح والكسر - آخره، سُمي به لاستتار القمر فيه، وقد استدل به الإمام أحمد على وجوب صوم يوم الشك، وعندنا هذا يفيد استحبابه لا وجوبه، لأنه
Chapter on what establishes the crescent and on fasting on the day of doubt and other (rulings). Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent or by completing Sha'ban as thirty (days) if the crescent is obscured. The day of doubt is: the day following the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban, and in it the two sides of knowledge and ignorance are equal, by the crescent being obscured. And all fasting is disliked in it except a voluntary fast, one that is decided upon without hesitation between it and another fast. Chapter: on what establishes the crescent and on fasting on the day of doubt and other (rulings). It is a communal obligation to seek the crescent on the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban at sunset, because it may be twenty-nine. Thus: Ramadan is established by sighting its crescent, due to his statement (ﷺ): 'Fast by sighting it, and break your fast by sighting it, and if it is obscured over you, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty' (1). Hence he said 'or by completing Sha'ban as thirty' days, 'if the crescent is obscured,' so it is not seen due to cloud or similar, because of what we narrated. And this is by consensus. And pointing to the crescent upon seeing it is disliked because it is an act of ignorance. In this is an indication that no consideration is given to the sayings of astrologers, so the crescent is not established by it, as we will mention. And he explained the day of doubt by his saying: The day of doubt is: what follows the twenty-ninth of Sha'ban, and in it the two sides of knowledge and ignorance are equal regarding the true state of affairs, by the crescent being obscured, i.e., the crescent of Ramadan, so it is possible that Sha'ban is complete or incomplete, in view of his statement: 'The month is thus, thus, and thus, and he tucked his thumb on the third time' (3), meaning twenty-nine, and his statement: 'thus, thus, thus' i.e., without tucking, meaning thirty. So doubt arises due to a hindrance, like cloud on the thirtieth day, whether it is from Ramadan or from Sha'ban. Al-Kamal said: Or the crescent of Sha'ban was obscured from Rajab and its count was completed, and the crescent of Ramadan was not seen, so doubt arises on the thirtieth of Sha'ban whether it is the thirtieth or the thirty-first, end. And Sheikh Imam Badr al-Din (r.a.) said: The hindrance is an attribute that [occurs] in the location without choice, and cloud, dust, smoke and the like, although they are entities, they prevent the observer from the observed, and this is an accidental preventing factor, as in al-Mustasfa. And all fasting is disliked in it, i.e., the day of doubt, from obligatory and compulsory (fasts), and a fast in which one hesitates between voluntary and other, except a voluntary fast that is decided upon without hesitation between it and another fast, for it (the fast) if it becomes apparent that it is Ramadan, it suffices for what he fasted. It is not disliked when it is in a manner that the common people do not know that, lest they become accustomed to fasting it and the ignorant think it is an addition to Ramadan. Thus al-Kamal restricted it. And if it coincides with a fast he used to fast, then fasting is better by consensus. And they differed on what is better if it does not coincide with his habit: Some say that breaking the fast is better as a precaution against the apparent prohibition, and some say that fasting is better, following 'A'isha and 'Ali, for they both used to fast it. Then, regarding what is disliked, the dislike varies. As for the dislike of fasting it as (if it is) from Ramadan, due to his statement (ﷺ): 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' (3), and in it is resemblance to the People of the Book in increasing the duration of the fast. If its being of Ramadan becomes apparent, it suffices him, and if he broke it and it became apparent that it was from Sha'ban, he does not make it up, like something presumed to be legislated that discharges. As for the dislike of the compulsory (fast), it is due to the form of the prohibition, like his prayer on another's land, but its dislike is less than the first due to lack of resemblance. If its being Ramadan becomes apparent, it suffices him if he is resident, and if he is a traveler, then (it suffices) from the compulsory according to the Imam. If it becomes apparent that it is from Sha'ban, then (it counts) according to what he intended, in the correct (view). As for the dislike of the voluntary (fast) with hesitation, it is because he intends the obligatory in one respect, by saying: If tomorrow is from Ramadan, (it counts) for it, otherwise it is supererogatory. And if it becomes apparent on the day of doubt that it is from Ramadan, what he fasted suffices for it, i.e., for Ramadan, with whatever intention (he had), except if he is a traveler and intended it for another compulsory fast, in the correct (view), as passed with our statement. If it becomes apparent that it is from Sha'ban, it is supererogatory without guarantee (of qada), because the element of discharging (obligation) entered his resolve in one respect. If he hesitated between a compulsory and a voluntary fast and it became apparent that it was from Sha'ban, it does not suffice for the compulsory because the aspect (of obligation) was not established due to hesitation, and the basic intention is not sufficient for him, and it becomes an obligatory (fast) not guaranteed by qada, due to his having started it as discharging (something). As for the absence of dislike for the voluntary fast that he decided upon, it is due to his statement to a man: 'Did you fast from the last part of Sha'ban?' He said: No. He said: 'Then when you break your fast, fast a day in its place.' (5) And 'sirar' of the month - with fatha and kasra - is its end, so named because of the concealment of the moon in it. Imam Ahmad used it as evidence for the obligation of fasting the day of doubt, and according to us, this indicates its recommendation, not obligation, because...
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter 'What Establishes the Crescent and Fasting on the Day of Doubt' from Nur al-Idah. The author begins by stating that fasting Ramadan is a communal obligation to seek the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban. The ruling for establishing the start of Ramadan is either by sighting the crescent (ru'ya) or, if obscured, by completing 30 days of Sha'ban. This is based on the famous hadith: 'Fast by sighting it and break your fast by sighting it; if it is obscured, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty.' The author notes consensus on this. He then explains the definition of yawm al-shakk (the day of doubt): it is the 30th day when the crescent is obscured, creating uncertainty whether it is the 30th of Sha'ban or the 1st of Ramadan. The Hanafis rely on the hadith of the Prophet showing the month as 29 or 30 days. The passage details the types of fasting on this day. Fasting with the intention of Ramadan is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it resembles the People of the Book and is disobedience. Fasting for a wajib (obligatory make-up) fast is also disliked but to a lesser degree. Fasting as a nafl with hesitation (saying 'if it is Ramadan, then for Ramadan, otherwise nafl') is disliked because it mixes intentions. However, a purely voluntary fast (nafl jazzam) without any linking to Ramadan is not disliked; this is supported by the hadith about fasting the last days of Sha'ban. If one fasts on yawm al-shakk and it later turns out to be Ramadan, the fast counts for Ramadan (for a resident); if a traveler intended a different wajib fast, it counts for that. If it turns out to be Sha'ban, the fast is nafl and no qada is required, except for the case of hesitation where it does not count for the intended wajib. The author also mentions a difference of opinion on what is better when yawm al-shakk does not coincide with a habitual fast: some prefer to break (to avoid the prohibition) while others prefer to fast (following 'Aisha and Ali). The passage ends by noting that Imam Ahmad used a hadith to argue for obligatory fasting on yawm al-shakk, but the Hanafi madhhab maintains it is only recommended (mustahab) due to the absence of a clear command.

Key Terms
الهلال (al-hilāl): The crescent moon at the beginning of the lunar month, sighting of which establishes the start of Ramadan.
يوم الشك (yawm al-shakk): The 30th day of Sha'ban when the crescent of Ramadan is obscured, so it is uncertain whether it is the last day of Sha'ban or the first of Ramadan.
كراهة (karāhah): Dislike; a legal classification between halal and haram. In this text, it includes both makruh tahrimi (prohibited dislike) and makruh tanzihi (lesser dislike).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the definition of yawm al-shakk?
A) The 29th of Sha'ban when the moon is not seen.
B) The 30th day of Sha'ban when the crescent of Ramadan is obscured, creating doubt.
C) Any day when one is unsure about the start of Ramadan.
D) The day after the 30th of Sha'ban when the crescent is sighted.

Key Takeaway
Ramadan is established only by sighting the crescent or completing 30 days of Sha'ban; yawm al-shakk is the 30th day when the crescent is obscured.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
15 min
The Degrees of Dislike for Fasting on the Day of Doubt
Explains rulings and proofs for different types of fasting on yawm al-shakk

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the different levels of karahah for fasting on yawm al-shakk and identify which intentions make a fast valid or invalid.

Core Idea
Fasting on the day of doubt is disliked except a decisive voluntary fast; the degree of dislike depends on the intention.

Now that we know what the day of doubt is, this passage details the rulings for fasting on it. The Hanafi school grades the dislike based on the type of fast one intends, with severe dislike for intending Ramadan itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four types of fasting on yawm al-shakk
The text mentions: fasting with intention of Ramadan, fasting for a wajib make-up, fasting with hesitation (if Ramadan then for Ramadan else nafl), and a decisive voluntary fast (nafl jazzam). List them.
The decisive voluntary fast is the only one not disliked.
2
Understand the hadith of prohibition
The hadith 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' is cited for the severe dislike of fasting as if it were Ramadan.
This hadith provides the proof for karahah tahrimi.
3
Analyze the rationale for each degree of karahah
Fasting as Ramadan includes resemblance to People of the Book, hence severe. Wajib fast has no resemblance but is still disliked because of the general prohibition. Hesitant nafl is disliked due to mixing intentions. Decisive nafl is not disliked because it is a separate act of worship.
The text explicitly cites the hadith and explains the reasoning.
4
Note the exceptional case of habitual fast
If the day of doubt coincides with a regular voluntary fast (e.g., Monday/Thursday), it is better to fast by consensus.
This is an exception to the dislike.
5
Understand the madhhab dispute with Imam Ahmad
Imam Ahmad considers fasting on yawm al-shakk obligatory based on another hadith. Hanafis interpret that hadith as recommendation (nadb), not obligation.
The thamarah: Hanafis allow breaking the fast without sin; Ahmad would consider it sinful to break.

فصل: فيما يثبت به الهلال وفي صوم يوم الشك وغيره
يجب على الكفاية التماس الهلال في التاسع والعشرين من شعبان وقت الغروب؛ لأنـه قـد يكون تسعة وعشرين، فلذا: ( يثبت رمضان برؤية هلالِهِ) لقوله : ( صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ، وَأَفْطِرُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ، فَإِنْ غُمَّ عَلَيْكُمْ، فَأَكْمِلُوا عِدَّةَ شَعْبَانَ ثَلاثِينَ ) (۱) فلذا قال أوْ بِعَد شعبان ثلاثين) يوماً، (إنْ غُمَّ الهلال)، فلم يُرَ لغيم ونحوه لما روينا، وهذا بالإجماع، وتكره الإشارة إلى الهلال عند رؤيته لأنه فعل الجاهلية، وفي هذا إشارة إلى أنه لا عبرة بقول المنجمين فلا يثبت به الهلال كما سنذكره. (و) بين (يوم الشَّكُ) بقوله : ويوم الشك ( هو : ما يلي التاسع والعشرين من شعبان، وقد استوى فيه طَرَفُ العلمِ والجَهْلِ) بحقيقة الحال ( بأن غُمَّ الهلالُ) أي: هلال رمضــان فاحتمل كمــال شــعـبـان، أو نقصانه نظراً لقوله : « الشَّهْرُ هَكَذَا وَهَكَذَا وَهَكَذَا وَخَنَسَ إِبْهَامَهُ فِي المَرَّةِ الثَالِثَةِ » (۳)، يعني: تسعة وعشرين وقوله: هكذا وهكذا وهكذا أي من غير خنس يعني: ثلاثين، فيشك بوجود علة، كغيم في اليوم الثلاثين أمن رمضان هو أو من شعبان ، قال ( الكمال » : أو يغم من رجب هلال شعبان فأكملت عدته ولم يكن رؤي هلال رمضان، فيقع الشك في الثلاثين من شعبان، أهو الثلاثون أو الحـادي والثلاثون انتهى. وقال الشيخ الإمام بدر الدين رحمه الله: العلة وصف [ يحل ] بالمحل لا عن اختيار، والغيم والغبار والدخان ونحوه، وإن كان عيناً غير أنه يمنع الرائي من المنظور إليه، وهذا عرض على أنه مانع كذا في ( المستصفى». Then, regarding what is disliked, the dislike varies. As for the dislike of fasting it as (if it is) from Ramadan, due to his statement (ﷺ): 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abu al-Qasim' (3), and in it is resemblance to the People of the Book in increasing the duration of the fast. If its being of Ramadan becomes apparent, it suffices him, and if he broke it and it became apparent that it was from Sha'ban, he does not make it up, like something presumed to be legislated that discharges. As for the dislike of the compulsory (fast), it is due to the form of the prohibition, like his prayer on another's land, but its dislike is less than the first due to lack of resemblance. If its being Ramadan becomes apparent, it suffices him if he is resident, and if he is a traveler, then (it suffices) from the compulsory according to the Imam. If it becomes apparent that it is from Sha'ban, then (it counts) according to what he intended, in the correct (view). As for the dislike of the voluntary (fast) with hesitation, it is because he intends the obligatory in one respect, by saying: If tomorrow is from Ramadan, (it counts) for it, otherwise it is supererogatory. And if it becomes apparent on the day of doubt that it is from Ramadan, what he fasted suffices for it, i.e., for Ramadan, with whatever intention (he had), except if he is a traveler and intended it for another compulsory fast, in the correct (view), as passed with our statement. If it becomes apparent that it is from Sha'ban, it is supererogatory without guarantee (of qada), because the element of discharging (obligation) entered his resolve in one respect. If he hesitated between a compulsory and a voluntary fast and it became apparent that it was from Sha'ban, it does not suffice for the compulsory because the aspect (of obligation) was not established due to hesitation, and the basic intention is not sufficient for him, and it becomes an obligatory (fast) not guaranteed by qada, due to his having started it as discharging (something). As for the absence of dislike for the voluntary fast that he decided upon, it is due to his statement to a man: 'Did you fast from the last part of Sha'ban?' He said: No. He said: 'Then when you break your fast, fast a day in its place.' (5) And 'sirar' of the month - with fatha and kasra - is its end, so named because of the concealment of the moon in it. Imam Ahmad used it as evidence for the obligation of fasting the day of doubt, and according to us, this indicates its recommendation, not obligation, because...
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the chapter 'What Establishes the Crescent and Fasting on the Day of Doubt' from Nur al-Idah. The author begins by stating that fasting Ramadan is a communal obligation to seek the crescent on the 29th of Sha'ban. The ruling for establishing the start of Ramadan is either by sighting the crescent (ru'ya) or, if obscured, by completing 30 days of Sha'ban. This is based on the famous hadith: 'Fast by sighting it and break your fast by sighting it; if it is obscured, then complete the count of Sha'ban as thirty.' The author notes consensus on this. He then explains the definition of yawm al-shakk (the day of doubt): it is the 30th day when the crescent is obscured, creating uncertainty whether it is the 30th of Sha'ban or the 1st of Ramadan. The Hanafis rely on the hadith of the Prophet showing the month as 29 or 30 days. The passage details the types of fasting on this day. Fasting with the intention of Ramadan is severely disliked (makruh tahrimi) because it resembles the People of the Book and is disobedience. Fasting for a wajib (obligatory make-up) fast is also disliked but to a lesser degree. Fasting as a nafl with hesitation (saying 'if it is Ramadan, then for Ramadan, otherwise nafl') is disliked because it mixes intentions. However, a purely voluntary fast (nafl jazzam) without any linking to Ramadan is not disliked; this is supported by the hadith about fasting the last days of Sha'ban. If one fasts on yawm al-shakk and it later turns out to be Ramadan, the fast counts for Ramadan (for a resident); if a traveler intended a different wajib fast, it counts for that. If it turns out to be Sha'ban, the fast is nafl and no qada is required, except for the case of hesitation where it does not count for the intended wajib. The author also mentions a difference of opinion on what is better when yawm al-shakk does not coincide with a habitual fast: some prefer to break (to avoid the prohibition) while others prefer to fast (following 'Aisha and Ali). The passage ends by noting that Imam Ahmad used a hadith to argue for obligatory fasting on yawm al-shakk, but the Hanafi madhhab maintains it is only recommended (mustahab) due to the absence of a clear command.

Key Terms
سرار الشهر (sirār al-shahr): The last part of the lunar month when the moon is hidden. In the context, it refers to the last days of Sha'ban.
كراهة تحريمية (karāhah taḥrīmiyyah): Prohibitive dislike; an action close to haram that should be avoided.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which type of fasting on yawm al-shakk is NOT disliked?
A) Fasting with the intention of Ramadan.
B) Fasting to make up a missed Ramadan day.
C) Fasting a decisive voluntary fast without hesitation.
D) Fasting with hesitation: 'If Ramadan, then for Ramadan; else nafl.'

Key Takeaway
The ruling on fasting on yawm al-shakk depends on intention: only a decisive voluntary fast is free from disapproval.

Sawm — Fasting

Fasting the Day of Doubt: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof and conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on fasting the day of doubt and explain why it is makruh tahrimi, using the hadith as proof.

Core Idea
Fasting the day of doubt as Ramadan is makruh tahrimi; but if it turns out to be Ramadan, the fast suffices.

The day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) is the 30th of Sha'ban when the new moon is not sighted. The Hanafi school distinguishes between fasting it with the intention of Ramadan (disliked) and fasting it as a supererogatory act (permissible). This lesson explores the ruling, its conditions, and the proof from the hadith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
The act is fasting on the 30th of Sha'ban when there is doubt. The ruling depends on the intention.
This is a conditional ruling based on the outcome.
2
Distinguish the two scenarios
If one fasts with the intention of Ramadan, it is makruh tahrimi. If one fasts as supererogatory (nafl) or due to a habitual fast, it is not disliked.
The dislike is due to resembling the People of the Book and the explicit hadith.
3
Examine the hadith proof
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abul Qasim.' In Hanafi usul, 'asa' indicates tahrim (prohibition), making the fast makruh tahrimi.
The hadith is in Bukhari and Muslim.
4
Understand the sufficiency when it is Ramadan
If it turns out to be Ramadan, the fast suffices for the obligatory Ramadan, because the intention was present, albeit with a prohibition.
The ruling is the same if the intention was conditional or general.
5
Note the consensus on habitual fasts
If the day of doubt coincides with a habitual fast (e.g., Monday/Thursday), fasting is better by consensus, and it is not disliked.
Al-Kamal restricted the dislike to cases where common people might be misled.

And if it becomes apparent that it is Ramadan, what he fasted suffices for it. It is not disliked if done in a manner that the common people do not know about and thus become accustomed to fasting it, so the ignorant think it is an addition to Ramadan. Al-Kamal restricted it thus. And if it coincides with a fast he used to observe, then fasting is better by consensus. They differed on what is better if it does not coincide with his habit: some said breaking the fast is better to avoid the apparent prohibition, and some said fasting is better, following 'Aisha and 'Ali, for they used to fast it. Then with regard to what is disliked, the degree of dislike varies. As for the dislike of fasting it as Ramadan, it is due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abul Qasim.' And in it there is resemblance to the People of the Book in increasing the duration of the fast. If its Ramadan-nature becomes apparent, it suffices him; if he broke it and it turned out to be from Sha'ban, he does not make it up, like something presumed for its legislativeness causing dropping. As for the dislike of the obligatory, it is due to the apparent prohibition like his prayer in another's land, but its dislike is less than the first due to the lack of resemblance. And if its Ramadan-nature became apparent, it suffices him if he is a resident; if a traveler, it is from the obligatory according to Imam. And if it turned out to be from Sha'ban, then according to what he intended in the correct view. As for the dislike of supererogatory with indecision, it is because he intends the obligatory in one respect, and that is he says: 'If tomorrow is from Ramadan, then it is for it; otherwise, it is supererogatory.' (And if it becomes apparent) on the day of doubt (that it is) from (Ramadan, what he fasted suffices for) it, i.e., for Ramadan (for him) with any intention, except if he is traveling and intended it for another obligatory in the correct view, as has preceded for what we said. And if it turns out to be from Sha'ban, it is a supererogatory not guaranteed, because the dropping entered his determination in one respect. And if he vacillated between obligatory and supererogatory and it turned out to be from Sha'ban, it does not count for the obligatory because the aspect was not established due to the hesitation, and the basic intention is not sufficient; and it is a fard not guaranteed by making up, because he started it as dropping. As for the absence of dislike for the supererogatory that he determined, it is due to his saying to the man: 'Did you fast from the last part of Sha'ban?' He said, 'No.' He said, 'Then if you break the fast, fast one day in its place.' And sirar of the month – with fatha and kasra – is its last part, so named because the moon is hidden in it. Imam Ahmad deduced from this the obligation of fasting the day of doubt, and with us this indicates its recommendation, not obligation, because it (the hadith) is opposed by the prohibition of preceding (Ramadan) by fasting a day or two. So it is interpreted to mean preceding by intention of Ramadan, to harmonize as much as possible, and the hadith of sirar becomes for recommendation. For the rational meaning in it is to end Sha'ban with worship, as that is recommended in every month. And [PAGE_630] If he vacillates in it between fasting and breaking, he is not considered fasting. And fasting a day or two from the end of Sha'ban is disliked. The proofs are opposed by the prohibition of preceding with a day or two of fasting. So it is interpreted to mean preceding with the fast of Ramadan, combining the texts as much as possible, and the hadith of sirar becomes for recommendation, because the rational meaning in it is to end Sha'ban with worship, as that is recommended in every month. It is a statement that this matter – ending the month with the worship of fasting – is not specific to Sha'ban, as might be assumed due to the connection of the obligatory fast with it, unlike interpreting the hadith of preceding as referring to supererogatory fasting. Then the prohibited would be supererogatory and the obligatory fast of Ramadan is established by the sirar hadith. So the prohibition of supererogatory is due to neglecting the obligation indicated by the sirar hadith, because it leads to opening the evil of presuming an addition to Ramadan when repeated with prevailing ignorance, and that is disbelief, because it is a lie against Allah regarding what He legislated, as the People of the Book did when they increased the duration of their fast. Thus what we have gone to is established: the permissibility of fasting it concealed from the common people. It cannot be said: His saying, 'The day that is doubted to be from Ramadan should not be fasted except as supererogatory' is a negative form, and it implies non-permissibility, because it is in the sense of prohibition due to its being realized sensually, and it implies legislativeness, as in al-'Inaya. (And if) a person (vacillates in) it, i.e., the doubt, (between fasting and breaking), like saying: 'If it is from Ramadan then I am fasting, otherwise I am breaking' (he is not considered fasting) because he did not resolve his determination, so it becomes like one who intends: 'If I find dinner tomorrow I will break, otherwise I will fast.' So if time passes like this and then its Ramadan-nature becomes apparent, he must make it up. Then he began to explain preceding the fast without doubt as a precaution, so he said: (And it is disliked to fast a day or two from the end of Sha'ban) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not precede the month by a day or two, except a man who was fasting a fast, so let him fast that day.' Agreed upon. And in al-Fawa'id: The meaning of his saying 'Do not precede the month by a day or two' is preceding with fasting thinking it is from Ramadan, because preceding one thing with another means intending it before its time and season. Sha'ban is the time for supererogatory, so if one fasts for Sha'ban, he has not come with the fast of Ramadan before its time, so this is not a preceding of it. Thus in the handwriting of our teacher al-Muhibi, may Allah have mercy on him. And in that there is advancing the ruling before the cause, which is invalid, as in al-'Inaya. Just as advancing Zuhr before Zuhr with intention of Zuhr, not another prayer, is not permissible, as in al-Diraya. And it is only disliked if with that intention.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, deals with the rulings on fasting the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) and the end of Sha'ban. It begins by stating that if one fasts on the day of doubt and it turns out to be Ramadan, that fast suffices for the obligatory Ramadan fast. Then it discusses the levels of dislike (karahah) in fasting: Fasting the day of doubt as if it were Ramadan is severely disliked due to the hadith 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abul Qasim' and because it resembles the People of the Book's addition to the fast. However, if one fasts on that day coinciding with a habitual fast (e.g., Monday/Thursday) or as a supererogatory fast without intending Ramadan, it is not disliked. There is also a discussion about the intention: if one makes a conditional intention (e.g., 'If this is Ramadan, then it is for Ramadan, otherwise it is supererogatory'), the fast is valid and sufficient if it turns out to be Ramadan, but if it turns out to be Sha'ban, it counts as supererogatory. If one vacillates between fasting and not fasting (e.g., 'If it is Ramadan, I am fasting; if not, I am not fasting'), he is not considered fasting at all, and must make up if it is Ramadan. The passage then addresses fasting the last day or two of Sha'ban: it is disliked to do so with the intention of Ramadan or as a precaution, but if one has a habitual fast, it is allowed. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith 'Do not precede the month by a day or two' and interprets it as prohibition of fasting with the intention of Ramadan. The opinion of Imam Ahmad that it is obligatory is rejected; the Hanafis hold it is recommended to fast the last part of Sha'ban as worship. The passage emphasizes the distinction between the dislike of fasting the day of doubt as Ramadan and the lack of dislike when fasting it as supererogatory, and clarifies that the prohibition is to prevent the ignorant from thinking an extra day is added to Ramadan.

Key Terms
يَوْمُ الشَّكِّ (yawm al-shakk): The day of doubt, i.e., the 30th of Sha'ban when the new moon of Ramadan is not sighted due to clouds or other reasons.
سِرَارُ الشَّهْرِ (sirar al-shahr): The last part of the month, specifically the last day or two of Sha'ban, so called because the moon is hidden at that time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is true about fasting the day of doubt in the Hanafi school?
A) Fasting it as Ramadan is wajib.
B) Fasting it as Ramadan is makruh tahrimi.
C) Fasting it as supererogatory is haram.
D) The fast never suffices for Ramadan.

Key Takeaway
Fasting the day of doubt as Ramadan is makruh tahrimi, but if it turns out to be Ramadan, the fast suffices.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate

Intention Scenarios on the Day of Doubt
Expansion of intention rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the validity of fasting on the day of doubt based on different intention formulations, including conditional and vacillating intentions.

Core Idea
A conditional intention suffices for the fast; vacillating between fasting and breaking invalidates it entirely.

The intention (niyyah) is crucial in fasting the day of doubt. The Hanafi school details three scenarios: (1) fasting with a conditional intention (e.g., 'If this is Ramadan, it is for Ramadan; otherwise nafl'), (2) fasting with a general intention of worship, and (3) vacillating between fasting and breaking. This lesson examines the validity and effect of each.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three intention types
The passage discusses: (a) conditional intention (if Ramadan then fard, else nafl), (b) general intention without condition, and (c) vacillating intention (if this day is Ramadan then I am fasting, else I am not).
Each has a different ruling on validity and sufficiency.
2
Analyze the conditional intention
If one says 'If tomorrow is Ramadan, this is for Ramadan; otherwise it is supererogatory,' and it turns out to be Ramadan, the fast suffices. If it is Sha'ban, it counts as nafl.
The intention is considered to include both possibilities.
3
Examine the vacillating intention
If one says 'I am fasting if it is Ramadan, not fasting if it is Sha'ban,' he is not considered fasting at all. If it turns out to be Ramadan, he must make up the day.
This is because the intention is not firm; he did not actually begin fasting with certainty.
4
Apply the rule to the general intention
If one fasts with the general intention of worship (e.g., nafl) without specifying Ramadan, and it turns out to be Ramadan, it does not count for Ramadan unless he had the specific intention for Ramadan initially.
The general nafl intention cannot substitute for the fard intention.
5
Summarize the sufficiency conditions
For the fast to count for Ramadan if it turns out to be Ramadan, the intention must at least include the possibility of Ramadan (conditional or explicit). Pure nafl intention does not suffice.
The exception is if the fasting was due to a habitual fast, then it is considered as if intended for Ramadan if it turns out to be Ramadan.

And if it becomes apparent that it is Ramadan, what he fasted suffices for it. It is not disliked if done in a manner that the common people do not know about and thus become accustomed to fasting it, so the ignorant think it is an addition to Ramadan. Al-Kamal restricted it thus. And if it coincides with a fast he used to observe, then fasting is better by consensus. They differed on what is better if it does not coincide with his habit: some said breaking the fast is better to avoid the apparent prohibition, and some said fasting is better, following 'Aisha and 'Ali, for they used to fast it. Then with regard to what is disliked, the degree of dislike varies. As for the dislike of fasting it as Ramadan, it is due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abul Qasim.' And in it there is resemblance to the People of the Book in increasing the duration of the fast. If its Ramadan-nature becomes apparent, it suffices him; if he broke it and it turned out to be from Sha'ban, he does not make it up, like something presumed for its legislativeness causing dropping. As for the dislike of the obligatory, it is due to the apparent prohibition like his prayer in another's land, but its dislike is less than the first due to the lack of resemblance. And if its Ramadan-nature became apparent, it suffices him if he is a resident; if a traveler, it is from the obligatory according to Imam. And if it turned out to be from Sha'ban, then according to what he intended in the correct view. As for the dislike of supererogatory with indecision, it is because he intends the obligatory in one respect, and that is he says: 'If tomorrow is from Ramadan, then it is for it; otherwise, it is supererogatory.' (And if it becomes apparent) on the day of doubt (that it is) from (Ramadan, what he fasted suffices for) it, i.e., for Ramadan (for him) with any intention, except if he is traveling and intended it for another obligatory in the correct view, as has preceded for what we said. And if it turns out to be from Sha'ban, it is a supererogatory not guaranteed, because the dropping entered his determination in one respect. And if he vacillated between obligatory and supererogatory and it turned out to be from Sha'ban, it does not count for the obligatory because the aspect was not established due to the hesitation, and the basic intention is not sufficient; and it is a fard not guaranteed by making up, because he started it as dropping. As for the absence of dislike for the supererogatory that he determined, it is due to his saying to the man: 'Did you fast from the last part of Sha'ban?' He said, 'No.' He said, 'Then if you break the fast, fast one day in its place.' And sirar of the month – with fatha and kasra – is its last part, so named because the moon is hidden in it. Imam Ahmad deduced from this the obligation of fasting the day of doubt, and with us this indicates its recommendation, not obligation, because it (the hadith) is opposed by the prohibition of preceding (Ramadan) by fasting a day or two. So it is interpreted to mean preceding by intention of Ramadan, to harmonize as much as possible, and the hadith of sirar becomes for recommendation. For the rational meaning in it is to end Sha'ban with worship, as that is recommended in every month. And [PAGE_630] If he vacillates in it between fasting and breaking, he is not considered fasting. And fasting a day or two from the end of Sha'ban is disliked. The proofs are opposed by the prohibition of preceding with a day or two of fasting. So it is interpreted to mean preceding with the fast of Ramadan, combining the texts as much as possible, and the hadith of sirar becomes for recommendation, because the rational meaning in it is to end Sha'ban with worship, as that is recommended in every month. It is a statement that this matter – ending the month with the worship of fasting – is not specific to Sha'ban, as might be assumed due to the connection of the obligatory fast with it, unlike interpreting the hadith of preceding as referring to supererogatory fasting. Then the prohibited would be supererogatory and the obligatory fast of Ramadan is established by the sirar hadith. So the prohibition of supererogatory is due to neglecting the obligation indicated by the sirar hadith, because it leads to opening the evil of presuming an addition to Ramadan when repeated with prevailing ignorance, and that is disbelief, because it is a lie against Allah regarding what He legislated, as the People of the Book did when they increased the duration of their fast. Thus what we have gone to is established: the permissibility of fasting it concealed from the common people. It cannot be said: His saying, 'The day that is doubted to be from Ramadan should not be fasted except as supererogatory' is a negative form, and it implies non-permissibility, because it is in the sense of prohibition due to its being realized sensually, and it implies legislativeness, as in al-'Inaya. (And if) a person (vacillates in) it, i.e., the doubt, (between fasting and breaking), like saying: 'If it is from Ramadan then I am fasting, otherwise I am breaking' (he is not considered fasting) because he did not resolve his determination, so it becomes like one who intends: 'If I find dinner tomorrow I will break, otherwise I will fast.' So if time passes like this and then its Ramadan-nature becomes apparent, he must make it up. Then he began to explain preceding the fast without doubt as a precaution, so he said: (And it is disliked to fast a day or two from the end of Sha'ban) due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'Do not precede the month by a day or two, except a man who was fasting a fast, so let him fast that day.' Agreed upon. And in al-Fawa'id: The meaning of his saying 'Do not precede the month by a day or two' is preceding with fasting thinking it is from Ramadan, because preceding one thing with another means intending it before its time and season. Sha'ban is the time for supererogatory, so if one fasts for Sha'ban, he has not come with the fast of Ramadan before its time, so this is not a preceding of it. Thus in the handwriting of our teacher al-Muhibi, may Allah have mercy on him. And in that there is advancing the ruling before the cause, which is invalid, as in al-'Inaya. Just as advancing Zuhr before Zuhr with intention of Zuhr, not another prayer, is not permissible, as in al-Diraya. And it is only disliked if with that intention.
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage from Imdad al-Fattah, a commentary on Nur al-Idah, deals with the rulings on fasting the day of doubt (yawm al-shakk) and the end of Sha'ban. It begins by stating that if one fasts on the day of doubt and it turns out to be Ramadan, that fast suffices for the obligatory Ramadan fast. Then it discusses the levels of dislike (karahah) in fasting: Fasting the day of doubt as if it were Ramadan is severely disliked due to the hadith 'Whoever fasts the day of doubt has disobeyed Abul Qasim' and because it resembles the People of the Book's addition to the fast. However, if one fasts on that day coinciding with a habitual fast (e.g., Monday/Thursday) or as a supererogatory fast without intending Ramadan, it is not disliked. There is also a discussion about the intention: if one makes a conditional intention (e.g., 'If this is Ramadan, then it is for Ramadan, otherwise it is supererogatory'), the fast is valid and sufficient if it turns out to be Ramadan, but if it turns out to be Sha'ban, it counts as supererogatory. If one vacillates between fasting and not fasting (e.g., 'If it is Ramadan, I am fasting; if not, I am not fasting'), he is not considered fasting at all, and must make up if it is Ramadan. The passage then addresses fasting the last day or two of Sha'ban: it is disliked to do so with the intention of Ramadan or as a precaution, but if one has a habitual fast, it is allowed. The Hanafi school relies on the hadith 'Do not precede the month by a day or two' and interprets it as prohibition of fasting with the intention of Ramadan. The opinion of Imam Ahmad that it is obligatory is rejected; the Hanafis hold it is recommended to fast the last part of Sha'ban as worship. The passage emphasizes the distinction between the dislike of fasting the day of doubt as Ramadan and the lack of dislike when fasting it as supererogatory, and clarifies that the prohibition is to prevent the ignorant from thinking an extra day is added to Ramadan.

Key Terms
النِّيَّةُ الْمُعَلَّقَةُ (al-niyyah al-mu'allaqah): A conditional intention, e.g., 'If this is Ramadan, it is fard; otherwise nafl.'
التَّرْدِيدُ (al-tardid): Vacillation between fasting and breaking, e.g., 'I will fast if it is Ramadan, else not.'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
On the day of doubt, a person says: 'I intend to fast if this day is from Ramadan, otherwise I have no intention to fast.' He fasts the whole day. According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is valid and counts for Ramadan if it turns out to be Ramadan.
B) The fast is invalid and must be made up (qada) even if it turns out to be Ramadan.
C) The fast is valid as a supererogatory fast regardless of the outcome.
D) The fast is makruh tahrimi and should be avoided.

Key Takeaway
A conditional intention (if Ramadan then fard else nafl) is valid; vacillating intention invalidates the fast entirely.

Sawm — Fasting
intermediate
8 min
Fasting the End of Sha'ban and the Madhhab Dispute
Ruling with proof and madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on fasting the last day(s) of Sha'ban, identify the proof, and evaluate the dispute with Imam Ahmad.

Core Idea
Fasting the last day(s) of Sha'ban is disliked only if done with the intention of Ramadan, not if it is a habitual or supererogatory fast.

The end of Sha'ban (sirar al-shahr) is a time when some Muslims fast out of caution for Ramadan. The Hanafi school rules that it is disliked to fast the last day or two with the intention of Ramadan, but not if one has a habitual fast or is making a general intention. This lesson also addresses the dispute with Imam Ahmad, who considered it obligatory based on the sirar hadith.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling on the last day(s) of Sha'ban
It is disliked (makruh) to fast a day or two at the end of Sha'ban with the intention of preceding Ramadan.
The proof is the hadith: 'Do not precede the month by a day or two...'
2
Examine the hadith prohibition
The hadith 'Do not precede the month by a day or two' is interpreted by Hanafis as prohibiting fasting with the intention of Ramadan, not as an absolute ban.
The exception is if one has a habitual fast, then it is allowed and even better.
3
Understand the sirar hadith
The Prophet ﷺ said: 'Fast one day in place of it' to a man who missed a day. This is taken by Hanafis as recommendation (istihbab) to end Sha'ban with worship, not obligation.
Imam Ahmad uses this hadith to argue for obligation (wujub).
4
Analyze the reconciliation
The two hadiths are harmonized by applying the prohibition to fasting with intention of Ramadan, and the sirar hadith to general supererogatory fasting at the end of Sha'ban.
This reconciliation avoids the contradiction and clarifies the ruling.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis may choose not to fast; Hanbalis must fast the day of doubt as a precaution.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi and preferred.

لا يكره إذا كان على وجه لا يعلم العوام ذلك فيعتادوا صومه فيظنه الجُهَّال زيادة على رمضان كــذا قيده « الكمال » ، وإذا وافق صوماً كان يصومه، فالصوم أفضل بالإجماع، واختلفوا في الأفضل إذا لم يوافق معتاده قيل: الأفضل الفطر احترازاً عن ظاهر النهي ) ، وقيل : الأفضل الصوم، اقتداءً بعائشة وعلي، فإنهما كانا يصومانه (۳)، ثم فيما يكره تتفاوت الكراهة. أما كـراهـة صـومـه عـلـى أنـه مـن رمضان فلقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم : « مَنْ صَامَ يَوْمَ الشَّكَ، فَقَدْ عَصَى أبَا الْقَاسِمِ (۳) وفيه تشبه بأهل الكتاب في زيادة مدة الصوم، فإن ظهرت رمضانيته أجزأه وإن افطره فظهر من شعبان لم يقضه، كالمظنون لمشروعيته مسقطاً، وأما كراهة الواجب فلصورة النهي كصلاته في أرض الغير، لكن كراهته دون الأول لـعــدم التشبه، ولو ظهر رمضانيته أجزأه لو مقيماً، ولو مسافراً فعن الواجب عند الإمام، ولو ظـهـر مـن شعبان فعماً نوى في الصحيح، وأما كراهة النفل مع الترديد فلأنه ناو للفـرض مـن وجـه، وهـو أن يقول: إن كان غداً من رمضان فعنه وإلا فتطوع، (وإن ظهر ) يوم الشك (أنـه) من (رمضان أجزاً عنه) أي: عن رمضان (ما صامَهُ) بأي نية كانت، إلا أن يكون مسافراً ونواه عن واجــب آخر في
(٤)
الصحيح، كما تقدم لما قلناه ، وإن ظهر من شعبان كان تطوعاً غير مضمون؛ لدخول الإسقاط في عزيمته من وجه، وإن ردَّد بين واجب ونفل وظهر من شعبان لم يجز عن الواجب لأن الجهة لم تثبت للتردد فيها، وأصل النية لا يكفيه، ويكون فرضاً غير مضمون بالقضاء، لشروعه فيه مسقطاً، وأما عدم كراهة التطوع الذي جزم به فلقوله ل الرجل : هَلْ صُمْتَ مِنْ سِرَارِ شَعْبَانَ؟ قال: لا، قال: فَإِذَا أفْطَرْتَ فَهُمْ يَوْمَاً مَكَانَهُ ) وسرار الشهر - بالفتح والكسر - آخره، سُمي به لاستتار القمر فيه، وقد استدل به الإمام أحمد على وجوب صوم يوم الشك، وعندنا هذا يفيد استحبابه لا وجوبه، لأنه
(۰)
(۱) وهو قوله : ( لا يتقدمن أحدكم رمضان بصوم يوم أو يومين إلا أن يكون رجل كان يصوم صوماً فليصم ذلــك اليوم»، أخرجه البخاري في الصوم، باب لا يتقدمن رمضان بصوم يوم ولا يومين (۱۹۱٤).
(۲) أخرجه البيهقي في السنن الكبرى (۲۱۱/٤).
(۳) أخرجه البخاري في الصوم، باب قول النبي : ( إذا رأيتم الهلال فصوموا، وإذا رأيتموه فأفطروا» (۱۹۰٦)، وأبو داود في الصيام، باب كراهية صوم يوم الشك (۲۳۳٤).
(٤) ص (٦٢٤).
(٥) أخرجه مسلم في الصيام، باب صوم سرر شعبان (۱۱٦۱)، وأبو داود في الصوم، باب: التقدم (۲۳۲۸)، وأحمد في مسنده (٤٢٨/٤).
