Conditions for Witnessing the Shawwal Moon
Conditions for Shawwal moon testimony clarified.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for accepting testimony for the new moon of Shawwal when the sky is cloudy and explain why they are stricter than for Ramadan.

Core Idea
Shawwal testimony requires explicit wording and two free witnesses; a single known witness may suffice only with detailed sighting explanation.

Proving the new moon of Shawwal is more stringent than for Ramadan to avoid prematurely ending the fast. The Hanafi school specifies conditions that ensure certainty. This passage from Imdad al-Fattah outlines those conditions, including the requirement for explicit testimony and the number of witnesses, as well as a special case for a single known witness if they provide a detailed account.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving testimony for the new moon of Shawwal. The ruling is that certain conditions must be met for its acceptance.
Testimony is a means of proof (bayyina).
2
List the conditions from the text
When sky is cloudy: explicit wording (lafẓ al-shahāda), two free men or one free man + two free women, no prior lawsuit needed.
These conditions are stricter than for Ramadan.
3
Note the difference from Ramadan
For Ramadan, one trustworthy witness suffices; Shawwal requires more.
Reason: ending Ramadan without certainty risks missing an obligatory fast.
4
Analyze the special ruling from Abu Bakr
A single known witness is accepted only if they explain seeing the moon enter and emerge from clouds.
This explanation dispels suspicion of error.
5
Understand the reasoning
Brief sighting possibility; explanation confirms unique observation.
Without explanation, testimony is rejected due to tuhma (suspicion).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط لهلالِ الفِطْر - إذا كان بالسّماءِ عِلَّةٌ لَفْظُ الشَّهادةُ منْ حُرَّيْنِ، أَوْ حُرِّ وحَرَّتَيْنِ ، بلا دعوى.. يشترطان في سائر الأخبار، كذا في « الخانية»، وأطلق في القبول كما في « الهدايـــة»، وقال صاحبها في « التجنيس والمزيد ) : وإن كانت السماء متغيّمة تقبل شهادة الواحد وهو معروف، وكان الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل يقول: إنما تُقبل شهادة الواحد إذا فسر فقال: رأيتـه فـي وقـت يدخل في السحاب ثم ينجلي، لأن الرؤية في مثل هذا تتفق في زمان قليل، فجاز أن ينفرد هو به، أما بدون هذا التفسير لا تقبل لمكان التهمة انتهى.
And the condition for the new moon of breaking fast – when there is an obstruction in the sky – is the wording of testimony from two free men, or one free man and two free women, without a lawsuit; they are required in other reports. Thus in al-Khaniyya. And acceptance is absolute as in al-Hidaya. Its author said in al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid: If the sky is cloudy, the testimony of one person is accepted if he is known. And the Shaykh Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl used to say: The testimony of one person is only accepted if he explains, saying: 'I saw it at a time when it entered the cloud and then emerged,' because sighting in such a case occurs in a short time, so it is possible that he alone saw it. Without this explanation, it is not accepted due to suspicion, end.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage specifies the conditions for proving the new moon of Shawwal (Eid al-Fitr) when the sky is cloudy. Unlike Ramadan, where a single trustworthy witness is sufficient, Shawwal requires stricter conditions: the witnesses must explicitly utter the wording of testimony (lafẓ al-shahāda), they must be two free men or one free man and two free women. Additionally, no prior lawsuit (daʿwa) is required, similar to other matters where testimony is accepted without a lawsuit. The author notes that some scholars, like in al-Hidaya, allow absolute acceptance of one witness if he is known. However, Imam Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl conditioned such acceptance on the witness specifying that he saw the moon enter a cloud and then emerge, because the moon's appearance can be fleeting; a detailed explanation dispels suspicion. Without this, testimony is rejected due to possible error. This ruling highlights the Hanafi emphasis on caution in confirming the start of a month, especially for ending Ramadan, to avoid breaking fast prematurely.

Key Terms
لفظ الشهادة (lafẓ al-shahāda): The explicit verbal declaration of testimony, e.g., 'I testify that I saw the new moon.'
التجنيس والمزيد (al-Tajnis wa al-Mazid): A Hanafi work by the author of al-Hidaya, Marghinani, containing additional rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Only if he is a renowned scholar.

Key Takeaway
Shawwal moon testimony, when cloudy, demands explicit wording and two witnesses; a single witness succeeds only with a detailed sighting account.

Relying on Astronomers for Moon Sighting: The Hanafi View
Hanafi ruling against astronomically determined moon sighting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on using astronomical calculations for moon sighting and explain the primary evidence from hadith.

Core Idea
Only actual sighting establishes the month; calculation is outside the Shariah's prescribed method.

This passage addresses a recurring issue: can astronomers' calculations replace visual confirmation of the new moon? The Hanafi school is clear that the lawgiver has tied fasting and breaking fast to actual sighting (ru'ya), not to mathematical precision. We will examine the main evidence, the minority view that accepts calculation, and the Hanafi response that equates reliance on astronomers to forbidden soothsaying.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the core ruling: the new moon is not established by astronomers (munajjimūn), and fasting does not become obligatory based on their statements.
The author begins with a note (tanbīh) to reinforce this principle.
2
Identify the opposing view and its proof
Recognise the minority view from later Shāfi‘īs like Taqī al-Dīn al-Subkī and a few Hanafis like Muḥammad ibn Muqātil: they accept calculation because it is definitive (qaṭ‘ī).
Al-Subkī even wrote a treatise leaning towards reliance on astronomers.
3
Analyse the Hanafi response
Examine al-Sarakhsī’s rebuttal: he calls the view far-fetched and cites the hadith against soothsayers, equating calculation with divination.
The key proof is the mutawātir hadith: 'Fast upon seeing it and break the fast upon seeing it.'
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilāf (practical consequence)
Understand the difference: if calculation is accepted, one could start or end Ramadan without sighting; the Hanafi school requires actual witness.
This affects millions of Muslims today when the moon is not sighted due to weather.
5
Identify the muftā bihī position
Confirm that the operative fatwa in the Hanafi school is to reject reliance on astronomers; only sighting or completing 30 days suffices.
The majority of Shāfi‘īs also agree, making this the stronger view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه: أشرنا باقتصارنا في الثبوت على ما ذكرنا إلى أنه لا يثبت الهلال بقول المنجمين المؤقتين، ولا يجب بقولهم الصيام، لأنه خارج عن نص الشارع: « صُومُوا لِرُؤْيَتِهِ وَأَفْطِرُوا لَرُؤْيَتِهِ ) وقد نظمه ابن وهبان فقال: [ من الطويل ] وقول أولي التوقيت ليس بموجب وقيل نعم والبعض إن كان يكثر د ) انتهى. وقال ابن الشحنة بعد نقل الخلاف فإذا اتفق أصحاب أبي حنيفة إلا النادر والشافعي أنه: لا اعتماد على قول المنجمين في هذا، ولمتأخري الشافعية الإمام « تقي الدين السبكي» في هذه المسالة تصنيف، مال فيه إلى اعتماد قول المنجمين لأن الحساب قطعي انتهى. ومن ذلك ما قال في التاتارخانية» عن « اليتيمة ) : لا بأس بالاعتماد على قول المنجمين، وعن محمد بن مقاتل : أنــه كان يسألهم ويعتمد على قولهم بعد أن يتفق على ذلك جماعة منهم، وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي» في كتاب الصوم: وقول من قال يرجع إلى قول أهل الحساب عند الاشتباه بعيد، فإن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: « مَنْ أَتَى كَاهِنَاً أو عَرَافَاً فَصَدَّقَهُ فِيْمَا يَقُولُ فَقَدْ كَفَرَ بِمَا أُنزِلَ عَلَى مُحَمَّدٍ ( )
Note: We indicated by our limitation of proof to what we mentioned that the new moon is not established by the statement of astronomers, nor does fasting become obligatory by their statement, because it is outside the text of the Lawgiver: 'Fast upon seeing it and break the fast upon seeing it.' And Ibn Wahban versified it: 'And the sayings of the time-keepers are not a cause for obligation, and it was said yes, but only if it is frequent.' End. And Ibn al-Shihna said after transmitting the disagreement: The companions of Abu Hanifa, except a rare few, and al-Shafi'i agree that there is no reliance on the astronomers' statements in this. Among the later Shafi'is, Imam Taqi al-Din al-Subki wrote a treatise on this issue, leaning towards relying on astronomers because calculation is definitive. And from that, it is said in al-Tatarhaniyya from al-Yatima: There is no harm in relying on the statement of astronomers. And from Muhammad ibn Muqatil: He used to ask them and relied on their statement after a group of them agreed. And Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi mentioned in the Book of Fasting: The statement of those who say to refer to people of calculus in case of doubt is far-fetched, for the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever goes to a soothsayer or diviner and believes what he says has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muhammad.'
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage addresses the use of astronomical calculations (qawl al-munajjimīn) for moon sighting. The author firmly states that the new moon is not established by astronomers' statements, nor does fasting become obligatory based on them, because the primary source is the hadith: 'Fast upon seeing it and break the fast upon seeing it.' This is the dominant Hanafi position and also that of al-Shafi'i, with few dissenting voices. However, some later scholars like Taqi al-Din al-Subki (Shafi'i) leaned towards calculation because they considered it definitive (qaṭʿī). There is also a minority Hanafi view, recorded in al-Tatarhaniyya from al-Yatima, that relying on astronomers is not harmful, and Muhammad ibn Muqatil even practiced asking them. But al-Sarakhsi strongly opposes this, equating reliance on astronomers with consulting soothsayers, citing the hadith that belief in such leads to disbelief. The operative fatwa in the Hanafi school is that calculation does not override actual sighting; the community must rely on physical witnesses.

Key Terms
منجم (munajjim): An astronomer who calculates the lunar months based on mathematical and astronomical data.
قطع (qaṭʿ): Certainty; here used to describe calculation as definitive (qaṭʿī) by its proponents.
توقيت (tawqīt): Time-keeping; setting precise times based on astronomical calculations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Astronomers are often disbelievers.
B) The hadith 'Fast upon seeing it' and the prohibition of consulting soothsayers.
C) Calculations are not precise enough.
D) There is no evidence; it is a matter of convenience.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school insists on visual sighting as the sole valid method to establish the lunar month, rejecting astronomical calculations even if deemed certain.

Conditions for Crescent Testimony with Cloud Cover and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Da'wa
Explains witness qualifications and rejection of astrology for crescent sighting.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for crescent testimony with cloud cover, identify the intra-Ḥanafī dispute on requiring a prior claim (daʿwā), and apply the ruling to reject astrological calculations for determining Ramaḍān.

Core Idea
Crescent testimony with cloud cover: two witnesses or one with detailed explanation; no prior claim needed; astrology rejected.

This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ delves into the technical conditions for establishing the crescent moon when the sky is overcast. It not only outlines the required witnesses but also reveals a nuanced disagreement among the early Ḥanafī masters regarding a prior legal claim. Furthermore, it firmly excludes astrological calculations as a valid method, grounding all obligations on direct sighting or empirical testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and context
Determine the ruling: establishing the crescent of Eid al-Fitr (or other crescent) when the sky has a cloud cover (ʿilla). The passage gives specific conditions for this scenario.
The same conditions apply to other crescents (e.g., Ramaḍān) by analogy.
2
State the default witness conditions
The basic requirement: testimony from two free men or one free man and two free women, uttered with the wording of testimony. The witnesses must be Muslim, morally upright, and not subject to ḥadd for false accusation.
No prior claim (daʿwā) is required according to the relied-upon position.
3
Note the special opinion for a single witness
If only one witness comes forward, his testimony is accepted only if he explains that he saw the moon enter and then emerge from the clouds. This is because such sighting occurs in a short time, so it is possible he alone observed it.
Without this explanation, his testimony is rejected due to suspicion (tuhma).
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on prior claim (daʿwā)
Abū Ḥanīfa requires a prior claim (daʿwā) for the crescent of both Ramaḍān and Fitr, analogizing to other testimonies. Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad do not require it, analogizing to testimony for emancipation of a slave or divorce of a free woman. The later authorities (al-Kamāl, Qāḍī Khān) favor the latter view, making it the muftā bihi.
The dispute is legitimate and accepted within the school; the practical ruling dispenses with the claim for necessity.
5
Evaluate the rejection of astrology
The crescent cannot be established by the statements of astrologers (munajjimīn), nor does fasting become obligatory by them. This is based on the Prophetic command: 'Fast upon its sighting and break your fast upon its sighting' and the ḥadīth warning against believing soothsayers. A minority (e.g., al-Subkī among Shāfiʿīs) argued for acceptance based on certainty of calculation, but the overwhelming Ḥanafī position rejects this.
Shams al-Aʾimma al-Sarakhsī called the opposing view 'far-fetched'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشرط لهلال الفطر إذا كان بالسماء علة لفظ الشهادة من حرين أو حر وحرمتين بلا دعوى يشترطان في سائر الأخبار كذا في الخانية وأطلق في القبول كما في الهداية وقال صاحبها في التجنيس والمزيد وإن كانت السماء متغيمة تقبل شهادة الواحد وهو معروف وكان الشيخ الإمام أبو بكر محمد بن الفضل يقول إنما تقبل شهادة الواحد إذا فسر فقال رأيته في وقت يدخل في السحاب ثم ينجلي لأن الرؤية في مثل هذا تتفق في زمان قليل فجاز أن ينفرد هو به أما بدون هذا التفسير لا تقبل لمكان التهمة انتهى. تنبيه: أشرنا باقتصارنا في الثبوت على ما ذكرنا إلى أنه لا يثبت الهلال بقول المنجمين المؤقتين ولا يجب بقولهم الصيام لأنه خارج عن نص الشارع صوموا لرؤيته وأفطروا لرؤيته وقد نظمه ابن وهبان فقال: [ من الطويل ] وقول أولي التوقيت ليس بموجب وقيل نعم والبعض إن كان يكثر انتهى. وقال ابن الشحنة بعد نقل الخلاف فإذا اتفق أصحاب أبي حنيفة إلا النادر والشافعي أنه لا اعتماد على قول المنجمين في هذا ولمتأخري الشافعية الإمام تقي الدين السبكي في هذه المسالة تصنيف مال فيه إلى اعتماد قول المنجمين لأن الحساب قطعي انتهى. ومن ذلك ما قال في التاتارخانية عن اليتيمة لا بأس بالاعتماد على قول المنجمين وعن محمد بن مقاتل أنه كان يسألهم ويعتمد على قولهم بعد أن يتفق على ذلك جماعة منهم وذكر شمس الأئمة السرخسي في كتاب الصوم وقول من قال يرجع إلى قول أهل الحساب عند الاشتباه بعيد فإن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال من أتى كاهنا أو عرافا فصدقه فيما يقول فقد كفر بما أنزل على محمد وشرط لهلال الفطر أي لثبوته وكذا لثبوت غيره من الأهلة إذا كان بالسماء علة لفظ الشهادة الصادرة بلفظها من حرين مكلفين مسلمين غير محدودين في قذف أو حر وحرمتين لكن بلا اشتراط تقدم دعوى على الشهادة كعتق الأمة وطلاق الحرة كذا في شرح الكنز للديري وقال الكمال عن قاضي خان وأما الدعوى فينبغي أن لا تشترط كما في عتق الأمة وطلاق الحرة عند الكل وعتق العبد في قول أبي يوسف ومحمد وأما على قياس قول أبي حنيفة فينبغي أن تشترط الدعوى في هلال الفطر وهلال رمضان انتهى. وذكر هذا قاضي خان بعدما جزم بأنه لا تشترط الدعوى في هلال رمضان كما قدمناه ثم قال الكمال وعلى هذا فما ذكروا من أن من رأى هلال رمضان في الرستاق وليس هناك وال ولا قاض فإن كان ثقة يصوم الناس بقوله وفي الفطر إذا أخبر عدلان برؤية الهلال أي وبالسماء علة لا بأس بأن يفطروا ويكون الثبوت فيه بلا دعوى وحكم للضرورة أرأيت لو لم ينصب في الدنيا إمام ولا قاض حتى عصوا بذلك أما كان يصام بالرؤية فهذا الحكم في محال وجوده انتهى. وعلله في التجنيس بأن قوله أي العدل دليل ظاهر ولم يعارضه رد القاضي فجاز الأخذ به.
And the condition for the crescent of Fitr: if there is a cause in the sky, the wording of testimony from two free men, or one free man and two free women, without a prior claim; these conditions are required in all other testimonies, as in al-Khaniyya. And acceptance is unrestricted as in al-Hidaya. The author of al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd said: If the sky is cloudy, the testimony of one man is accepted, and this is well-known. Shaykh al-Imām Abū Bakr Muḥammad ibn al-Faḍl said: The testimony of one is only accepted if he explains by saying, 'I saw it at a time when it entered the cloud then emerged,' because sighting in such a case occurs in a short time, so it is possible that he alone observed it. Without this explanation, it is not accepted due to potential suspicion. Caution: We indicated by limiting proof to what we mentioned that the crescent is not established by the statement of astrologers, nor is fasting obligatory by their statement, because it is outside the text of the Lawgiver: 'Fast upon its sighting and break your fast upon its sighting.' Ibn Wahbān versified it: 'The statement of the timers is not binding, and it was said yes, and some if it is abundant.' Ibn al-Shiḥna said after narrating the disagreement: The Companions of Abū Ḥanīfa, except the rare, and al-Shāfiʿī agree that there is no reliance on the statement of astrologers in this. Among later Shāfiʿīs, Imam Taqī al-Dīn al-Subkī wrote a treatise on this issue, inclining toward relying on the statement of astrologers because calculation is certain. From that, it is said in al-Tātārkhāniyya from al-Yatīma: There is no harm in relying on the statement of astrologers. From Muḥammad ibn Muqātil: He used to ask them and rely on their statement after a group of them agreed on it. Shams al-Aʾimma al-Sarakhsī mentioned in Kitāb al-Ṣawm: The statement of one who says reference is made to the people of calculation in cases of doubt is far-fetched, for the Prophet ﷺ said: 'Whoever goes to a soothsayer or fortune-teller and believes what he says has disbelieved in what was revealed to Muḥammad.' And the condition for the crescent of Fitr, i.e., for its establishment, and likewise for the establishment of other crescents, if there is a cause in the sky, is the wording of testimony issued by its wording from two free, legally responsible Muslims not subject to ḥadd for false accusation, or one free man and two free women, but without the condition of a prior claim upon the testimony, like the emancipation of a slave woman and the divorce of a free woman, as in Sharḥ al-Kanz al-Dayrī. Al-Kamāl said from Qāḍī Khān: As for the claim, it should not be required, as in the emancipation of a slave woman and the divorce of a free woman according to all, and the emancipation of a slave according to Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad. But according to the analogy of Abū Ḥanīfa's statement, the claim should be required for the crescent of Fitr and the crescent of Ramaḍān. Qāḍī Khān mentioned this after asserting that the claim is not required for the crescent of Ramaḍān as we have mentioned. Then al-Kamāl said: On this basis, what they mentioned that whoever sees the crescent of Ramaḍān in a rural area and there is no governor or judge there, if he is trustworthy, people fast upon his statement. In the case of Fitr, if two just men report the sighting of the crescent, i.e., with a cause in the sky, it is fine for them to break their fast, and establishment is without a claim as a ruling of necessity. Do you not see that if no imam or judge were appointed in the world, would they thereby disobey? Would they not fast upon sighting? This ruling is in the realm of its existence. And it is justified in al-Tajnīs by saying: His statement, i.e., the just man, is a clear proof and is not opposed by the rejection of the judge, so it is permissible to act upon it.
Source pages p. 634

Commentary
This passage from Imdād al-Fattāḥ explains the conditions for establishing the crescent moon when the sky is overcast (ʿilla). It begins with the matn that for the crescent of Eid al-Fitr, if the sky has a cloud cover, the testimony must be spoken by two free men or one free man and two free women, and no prior legal claim (daʿwā) is required. The commentator notes that these conditions are like those in other testimonies, citing al-Khāniyya and al-Hidāya. A notable opinion from al-Tajnīs wa al-Mazīd accepts a single witness if he provides a detailed explanation of seeing the moon enter and emerge from clouds; otherwise, it is rejected due to the possibility of error. A lengthy alert (tanbīh) rejects the validity of astronomical calculations for establishing the moon, emphasizing that the prophetic directive is to act upon sighting, not calculation. However, later scholars like Taqī al-Dīn al-Subkī (Shāfiʿī) argued for accepting calculations as certain, a view rejected by the majority of Ḥanafīs. The commentator then returns to the condition of a prior claim, revealing an intra-Ḥanafī dispute: Abū Ḥanīfa requires a claim for both Ramaḍān and Fitr, while Abū Yūsuf and Muḥammad do not require it for Ramaḍān and even for Fitr analogize to emancipation and divorce. The final citation from al-Tajnīs justifies accepting the testimony without a claim because the just person's statement is a clear proof not countered by a judge's rejection. Throughout, the commentary maintains the Ḥanafī position that the crescent is established by direct testimony from reliable Muslims, not by calculation or conjecture.

Key Terms
هلال الفطر (hilāl al-fiṭr): The crescent moon that marks the start of Shawwāl, signifying the end of Ramaḍān.
دعوى (daʿwā): A formal legal claim made before testimony; in this context, a claim made by the witness that they saw the moon.
منجم (munajjim): An astrologer who calculates astronomical positions to predict celestial events, including crescent visibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number of witnesses required to establish the crescent of Eid al-Fitr when the sky is overcast, according to the relied-upon Ḥanafī position?
A) One free man who explains his sighting
B) Two free men or one free man and two free women
C) A large multitude (al-jamʿ al-ʿaẓīm)
D) Fifty men, as in qasāma

Key Takeaway
The crescent for Ramaḍān and Fitr is established only by valid testimony (two men or one man with explanation when cloudy), without a prior claim, and never by astrological calculation.
